  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f8b46737-d4e4-4430-8077-bae7775c3482'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer11761591311158241896">Now in the final stages of their quest for his son, Garion and his companions travel to Kell to consult the only undamaged copy of the Malloreon Gospels.   <span id="freeText11761591311158241896" style="display:none">Now in the final stages of their quest for his son, Garion and his companions travel to Kell to consult the only undamaged copy of the Malloreon Gospels. For centuries the Seers have guarded this book from the Grolims and even had their wizards put a curse of blindness on any Grolim who tried to enter Kell.<br /><br />So, as proclaimed in Guardians of the West, Belgarion the Godslayer sets out with those who must join him: the Eternal Man, the Guide, the Man with Two Lives, the Bearer of the Orb and the Silent Man, and the rest of his companions to The Place Which Is No More to make the final choice - darkness or light.<br /><br />But Zandramas the Sorceress will not be outdone. Though she may not enter Kell she still has young Geran and should she reach the final meeting place with him, then Garion must slay his son or the world will be no more.<br /><br />THUS ENDS THE EPIC STORY OF THE MALLOREON</span>

<div id="review_1931413602" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1931413602" />
    <a title="Jane Jago" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54499726-jane-jago"><img alt="Jane Jago" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569092764p2/54499726.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1931413602?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Jago" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Jago" href="/user/show/54499726-jane-jago">Jane Jago</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1931413602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5066027245675776628">Right. I'm going to talk about all five books because I have just read them head-to-head so to speak.<br/><br/>First thing to say is I'm a fan of Eddings, and I don't subscribe to the view that there is anything at all wrong with writing stuff that is entertaining. So if you are expecting me to go off on one about how this would be better if it was darker, or how it adds nothing to the sum of human knowledge you are about to be very disappointed.<br/><br/>This is over all an entertaining quintet and I am fond of it</span>
  <span id="freeText5066027245675776628" style="display:none">Right. I'm going to talk about all five books because I have just read them head-to-head so to speak.<br /><br />First thing to say is I'm a fan of Eddings, and I don't subscribe to the view that there is anything at all wrong with writing stuff that is entertaining. So if you are expecting me to go off on one about how this would be better if it was darker, or how it adds nothing to the sum of human knowledge you are about to be very disappointed.<br /><br />This is over all an entertaining quintet and I am fond of its essential innocence. I also like the way it rolls along at a brisk clip-after a bit of a slow start in volume one. You know good will triumph in the end, and that's what you want if you opt to read so-caked soft fantasy.<br /><br />I am also enamoured of Eddings as a writer. He's good, and immerses you in his world without suffocating you.<br /><br />What I don't like is Polgara, who gets right up my nose -too much uber mother and superiority. I also find myself wishing that Garion was less nice. But that could be just me. <br /><br />All in all I'd recommend this as a warming winter read to be taken in front of a roaring fire with a dog on your feet.<br /><br />I still prefer the Sparhawk books, but I'll always go back and give The Belgariad and The Malloreon a read every now and again.<br /><br />Go on. You know you want to </span>
  <a data-text-id="5066027245675776628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1942552116" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1942552116" />
    <a title="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy"><img alt="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475772748p2/4702933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1942552116?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" href="/user/show/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy">MrsJoseph *grouchy*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345377593" href="/book/show/773523.The_Seeress_of_Kell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=2017-reading-challenges">2017-reading-challenges</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1942552116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12615072594022010998">*This review contains spoilers for the previous books in the series as well as very light spoilers for this book.<br/><br/><br/>Getting to the end of this series always makes me feel a bit pensive. Of course, since there are 11 books (total) in the Belgariad and the Mallorean, I see another re-read in my near future.<br/><br/>I have to say that I’m starting to think that The Seeress of Kell is my favorite book in this five book series. There’s so many parts that I just get a kick out of. <br/><br/>I love the bromance between Belg</span>
  <span id="freeText12615072594022010998" style="display:none">*This review contains spoilers for the previous books in the series as well as very light spoilers for this book.<br /><br /><br />Getting to the end of this series always makes me feel a bit pensive. Of course, since there are 11 books (total) in the Belgariad and the Mallorean, I see another re-read in my near future.<br /><br />I have to say that I’m starting to think that The Seeress of Kell is my favorite book in this five book series. There’s so many parts that I just get a kick out of. <br /><br />I love the bromance between Belgarion &amp; 'Zakath. I love how Garion keeps asking 'Zakath <i>"are you sure you're not an Arend?"</i> LOL! During the previous series Garion only had Ce'Nedra as a real friend and all the others were much, much older than he and always in a position of authority over him. <br /><br />Another one of my favorite parts is <i>everything</i> Dal Pevior (sp?). I adored basically every moment of that. :-D<br /><br />I also love everything with the wolves. My only issue with the wolves is that Eddings (once again) directly contradicts himself! Supposedly it impossible for wolves to lie because you cannot lie in thought. The wolf was shocked when she learned the man-things can tell untruths. Ok, so this is a rule. Not possible to lie. So why does Eddings show the female wolf lying quite often?! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ But later in the book the reader learns that Poledra is the female wolf - and she's been lying the entire time! How is this possible?<br /><br /> In <i>Sorceress of Darshiva</i> Belgarion asks <br /><blockquote><i>"Where is your mate?” <br />“He no longer runs or hurts. I visit his bone sometimes." </i><br />P210 <i>Sorceress of Darshiva</i> Omnibus edition </blockquote><br /><br />This is clearly false as Belgarath is her mate. He still runs and hunts - he is also alive so she can't 'visit his bones.'<br /><br /><blockquote><i>"This one is your mate," the she-wolf said. "I can smell your scent on her."<br /> "Yes," Garion agreed. <br />"She's very small. I see now why she can't hunt. Is she fully grown?"<br /> "Yes, she is." <br />"Has she had her first litter yet?" <br />"Yes."<br />" How many puppies?"<br />" One."<br />" One only?" The wolf sniffed. I have had as many as six. You should have chosen a larger mate. I'm sure she was the runt of her litter." </i><br />P214 <i>Sorceress of Darshiva</i> Omnibus edition</blockquote><br /><br />Another lie - Poledra has only birthed 2 children: the twins Polgara and Beldaren.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I wish [Eddings] would just make up his mind!<br /><br /><br />Not to forget my women characterization theme, let’s take a look at Vella. Vella is a Nadrak woman who is currently owned by Yarblek (Silk’s Nadrak partner). Vella is described as heartbreakingly lovely and extremely feisty. She typically dresses in tight leather pants with a tight leather vest and her multiple daggers on display. Occasionally Vella dresses in thin (almost translucent) Malloreon dress in order to dance (almost all Nadrak women dress this way to dance – and all the dances are for the entertainment of [large] groups of men. Supposedly this dance (which ends with a sensual strut) shows the woman’s power.) *rolls eyes*<br /><br /><br /><blockquote><i>The factor was a squinty-eyed Nadrak name is Zelmit, who was probably almost as untrustworthy as he looked. Vella had never really liked him and she customarily loosened her daggers in their sheaths whenever she came into his presence, making very sure that he saw her doing so to be certain that there would be no misunderstandings. Technically, of course, Vella was one of Yarblek's possessions, and Zelmit had a reputation for making rather free with the things that belong to his employer. </i><br />P317 Omnibus Edition</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote><i>Since the age of 12, she had always relied on her daggers to ward off any unwanted attention. Although she had seldom been obliged to kill anyone – except for a few enthusiasts – she had nonetheless established a reputation for being a girl no sensible man would attempt. Sometimes that rankled a bit, though, since there were times when Vella might have welcomed an attempt. A nick or two in some unimportant places upon an ardent admirer would sustain her honor, and then – well, who knows? </i><br />P319 Omnibus Edition</blockquote><br /><br />Moving on from Vella, let’s revisit Zandramas. As I mentioned (in a previous review), there appears to be some sort of parallel between promiscuity, nudity and being a woman antagonist. I feel like I’m not saying that right but hey, you get the drift. In almost every situation where there is a woman who isn’t Light, she’s also “a slut.” Good to know. <br /><br />When a demon was compelled to confess who he was “working for,” he replied…<br /><blockquote><i>"[redacted] and I contended with each other, in truth, but our contention was not on behalf of mad Urvon or <b>sluttish</b> Zandramas." </i><br />P438 Omnibus Edition </blockquote><br /><br />When Zandramas has a chance to try to beguile Belgarion into becoming a traitor to the Light, she immediately offers him sex:<br /><br /><blockquote><i>"...[Belgarion] canst put aside thine earthly wife, who is not, after all, human, and thou and I could mate. Thou couldst father a race of gods upon me, Belgarion, and we could sate each other with unearthly delights. Thou wilt find me fair, King of Riva, as all men have, and I will consume thy days with the passion of the gods, and we will share in the meeting of Light and Dark." </i><br />P444 Omnibus Edition </blockquote><br /><br />Of course, you almost never see slut shaming without the required consequences. In this situation, after Zandramas is defeated, she is stripped naked in front of her enemies. I felt that was overkill, to be honest. She’s already defeated – so why is it necessary to strip her naked? Are we just rubbing salt in the wound? I do concede that it wasn’t difficult to strip her naked – Eddings had her wearing only her Grolim robe (but it’s satin!) for the entire series. <br /><br /><blockquote><i>Zandramas shrank back even more. "Don't touch me," she said. <br /><br />"It is not thee I would touch, Zandramas , but thy raiment. I would see thee receive thy reward and thine exaltation." Poledra tore back the satin hood and ripped the black robe away. Zandramas made no attempt to conceal her nakedness, for indeed, there was no nakedness. </i> Omnibus Edition </blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12615072594022010998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_156866149" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156866149" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156866149?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Leon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Leon" href="/user/show/5128242-andrew-leon">Andrew Leon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156866149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9461645625588743297">It's great to re-visit the characters from The Belgariad and see them in action again; unfortunately, that's the best thing that can be said about the series. It's not that it's bad; it's a completely enjoyable read. However, Eddings fails to move forward with his writing and, instead, gives us what is essentially the same plot from The Belgariad over again. If you've read The Belgariad and loved it, you should certainly read The Mallorean, as well. If you're hoping for something new, though, mo</span>
  <span id="freeText9461645625588743297" style="display:none">It's great to re-visit the characters from The Belgariad and see them in action again; unfortunately, that's the best thing that can be said about the series. It's not that it's bad; it's a completely enjoyable read. However, Eddings fails to move forward with his writing and, instead, gives us what is essentially the same plot from The Belgariad over again. If you've read The Belgariad and loved it, you should certainly read The Mallorean, as well. If you're hoping for something new, though, move on to some other author. Eddings continues to re-hash the plot from The Belgariad throughout most of the rest of his writing career. The problem is that he never does it better than he did in The Belgariad, so there's no reason to read anything else.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9461645625588743297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2253465796" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2253465796" />
    <a title="Narilka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60022503-narilka"><img alt="Narilka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475501572p2/60022503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2253465796?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Narilka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Narilka" href="/user/show/60022503-narilka">Narilka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345377593" href="/book/show/773523.The_Seeress_of_Kell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60022503-narilka?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2253465796" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2407624727157634274"><b>"It has come at last," Garion's inner companion said unemotionally through the Child of Light's* lips. "It is the instant of the Choice. Choose, Cyradis, lest all be destroyed."<br/><br/>"It has come," another equally unemotional voice spoke through the lips of the Child of Dark*. "It is the instant of the Choice. Choose, Cyradis, lest all be destroyed."</b><br/><br/><i>The Seeress of Kell</i> is the fifth and final book in <i>The Malloreon</i> by David Eddings. And quite an end it is! The quest draws to a close as the final riddles</span>
  <span id="freeText2407624727157634274" style="display:none"><b>"It has come at last," Garion's inner companion said unemotionally through the Child of Light's* lips. "It is the instant of the Choice. Choose, Cyradis, lest all be destroyed."<br /><br />"It has come," another equally unemotional voice spoke through the lips of the Child of Dark*. "It is the instant of the Choice. Choose, Cyradis, lest all be destroyed."</b><br /><br /><i>The Seeress of Kell</i> is the fifth and final book in <i>The Malloreon</i> by David Eddings. And quite an end it is! The quest draws to a close as the final riddles are solved so the meeting of Light and Dark can happen to decide the fate of the world. Zandramas strives until the bitter end to thwart her opponent. Garion must stay resolute to prevent the world from sliding into darkness even if it means he must kill his own son.<br /><br />It is a great ending to the series. All story threads are wrapped up, including a couple items from book one that had been left dangling. I've been with these characters for so long now that they feel like old friends and it is the character dynamics that has been the most enjoyable part of my reread. Sometimes it's hard for an author to keep track of all the characters when a series focuses on a fairly large group and I'd say Eddings is successful at giving everyone their own voice. The ending does have its bittersweet moment though. I'm quite glad to have made the journey again and am a little sad for it to be over.<br /><br />*Quote changed slightly to prevent spoilers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2407624727157634274" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_404684384" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404684384" />
    <a title="David Sarkies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies"><img alt="David Sarkies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470027282p2/5856247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/404684384?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sarkies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sarkies" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies">David Sarkies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Nobody really</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to David by: </span>
      My auntie
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5856247-david-sarkies?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer404684384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4105474590962660870"><b>The final book in the pentology, or so we thought</b><br/>31 August 2012<br/><br/>	Well, I have now come to the end of another pointless series of books that does very little to add to the collection of human literature that is pounding our vision these days. A lot of people do seem to have liked these books and I must admit that when I was a teenager I was one of them, but these days I hope that books like these will end up being confined to the dust bin of history and forgotten like the many other books that hav</span>
  <span id="freeText4105474590962660870" style="display:none"><b>The final book in the pentology, or so we thought</b><br />31 August 2012<br /><br />	Well, I have now come to the end of another pointless series of books that does very little to add to the collection of human literature that is pounding our vision these days. A lot of people do seem to have liked these books and I must admit that when I was a teenager I was one of them, but these days I hope that books like these will end up being confined to the dust bin of history and forgotten like the many other books that have vanished over the centuries. It is interesting that I look just below this commentary (I keep backups of all my commentaries on a Word document) and I see Lucian of Samatosa. The reason that I mention him is that one of his pet annoyances was the ridiculous amount of literature that was being published around his time that would forever make him cringe. The difference is that the ancient Romans didn't have a printing press which meant that everything had to be copied by hand, which made books incredibly expensive. Today not only do we have printing presses, we also have computers, which gives us the ability to churn out rubbish like never before.<br />	I have already suggested that some people write because they want to become rich from what they consider to be an easy job. This is a delusion because first of all writing is not easy, and secondly, you are highly unlikely to become rich. Writing takes an awful lot of discipline, especially having to write at those times when you do not want to write. I admit that I like writing, but I have trouble disciplining myself to remain committed to one piece of work. I like writing fiction, but once again, there is the discipline not only to work on the story until it is completed, but to also structure it in a way that the characters are realistic and the story is consistent. In a way that I why I like these commentaries because, even though I do not get paid to write them, I am able to write down my thoughts and ideas in a way that allows me to consider new and different things based upon the book on which I am commenting, and I do not need to structure it in the same what that I would a novel. Also, the idea of creating a realistic character is not necessary, though the essence of discipline is still present. In a way I like writing because it allows me to put these thoughts down on paper (or rather, on the Internet) so that others can read them, and maybe be challenged by them as well.<br />	Anyway, I have not said anything about this book, and as I look at the time, I am unlikely to say anything on this book. All I have said is that this is the last book in the series, and I have said enough about the series in the other four books that I do not feel that it is necessary to repeat what I have already said. I still occasionally read fantasy novels, but most of them these days have fallen by the wayside. I am no longer interested in the Tolkeinesque style of adventure, and in many ways these attempted copies come nowhere near the brilliance of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/656983.J_R_R__Tolkien" title="J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">Tolkien</a>'s original works. I have read some Conan books recently, but that was more out of interest and to also experience some of the pre-Tolkien fantasy literature. Of course, there are also the books that have been written by friends, and in a way I would not be much of a friend if I did not read their books. However, when it comes to a novel these days I am generally looking for something different, and even then, most of those books end up staying in the bookshop rather than being transferred to by bookshelf (not that I have one at the moment). </span>
  <a data-text-id="4105474590962660870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12128294795693441027">I REALLY loved the Belgariad series, and I so looked forward to this follow up series. I had hoped it would be similar but with new story lines, and adventures.<br/><br/>Instead it was a bad rehash of the same story, but with the extra addition of some pretty ludicrous twists, that caused enough discontinuity with the original series, as to make it hardly worth reading.<br/><br/>You always hear about series that were continued in the blind search to squeeze more money out of fans of the original, and usually I thin</span>
  <span id="freeText12128294795693441027" style="display:none">I REALLY loved the Belgariad series, and I so looked forward to this follow up series. I had hoped it would be similar but with new story lines, and adventures.<br /><br />Instead it was a bad rehash of the same story, but with the extra addition of some pretty ludicrous twists, that caused enough discontinuity with the original series, as to make it hardly worth reading.<br /><br />You always hear about series that were continued in the blind search to squeeze more money out of fans of the original, and usually I think saying that is unfair. In this case though, it fits. I jumped in with both feet at the prospect of seeing what happens to some well loved characters, and what I got was a series of this already happened... Oh, and we'll change this and completely change what we already said happened before.<br /><br />I am aware of the literary and movie and television tool of "hanging a lantern" on things too unbelievable to pass, but Eddings hangs so many on this story line that it grew tired instead. </span>

<div id="review_2278931717" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2278931717" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22029917-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577772170p2/22029917.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2278931717?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/22029917-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22029917-sarah?shelf=easy-and-fun">easy-and-fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22029917-sarah?shelf=fantasy-and-adventure">fantasy-and-adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2278931717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12690923232345356021">This is a review for both the Malloreon and the Belgariad. <br/><br/>I used to love these books, they gave me the warm fuzzy feeling of books that you loved as a child and then kept reading as an adult. The first time I read them I must have been 12 years old. In some ways, the two series still resonate with me - I love the world-building. Eddings put so much into the world and its geography. He also did a fantastic job, for the most part, with the people. The cities and towns were a lot of fun, and rando</span>
  <span id="freeText12690923232345356021" style="display:none">This is a review for both the Malloreon and the Belgariad. <br /><br />I used to love these books, they gave me the warm fuzzy feeling of books that you loved as a child and then kept reading as an adult. The first time I read them I must have been 12 years old. In some ways, the two series still resonate with me - I love the world-building. Eddings put so much into the world and its geography. He also did a fantastic job, for the most part, with the people. The cities and towns were a lot of fun, and random people were well written. The concept of an ultimate good vs easy high fantasy story is also a lot of fun. It is easy to understand and the writing flows well. These are all great reasons to love the books. That being said, my most recent reread of these books brought forward and compounded all of the issues I have had overlooked in the past with these books. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />I feel like Eddings wanted a very "clean" world with well-defined boundaries and roles in society. This could play in his favor for a time, but it became tiresome to read instances of people behaving in a way contradictory to their national trait and so then that trait is questioned by the characters. The biggest and most problematic one came when the Alorns, and most importantly the Algars could only be kind to the Murgos after the peace accords because the king of the Murgos was actually an Alorn. The thing with this is that Eddings had worked hard to show Garion and his companions working hard to overcome their prejudices by exposure to these other groups, and if Eddings had continued along this vein with the rest of his countrymen it would have been more believable and agreeable. Also not giving personality-defining national traits probably would have helped. I can understand certain behaviors being typical in certain places because of how that society lives, but there is and should be a line. Not every Alorn needed to be blood thirsty and extremely into fighting, not all Murgos should be cruel and brutish, and why on earth were all of the Thulls dumb? I feel like these are almost caricatures of stereotypes. Another issue I had was the gender roles. I am not saying we had to have gender-bending or that no woman is allowed to enjoy traditional female roles or that no man can enjoy traditional male roles either. It was more like the comments that a woman did not act like a "typical woman" because she was smart or forward or could rule a country competently. I didn't like that none of the men could cook or that when any topic came up related to sex or childbirth the women would leave. This also brings me to the another point that irritated me no end: people deciding for others in the group (usually the women and younger men) what they did or did not want to know or see. If this was once in awhile, fine. But this was anytime there was a sex worker or, at one point Beldin, a man, was describing the process of pregnancy and childbirth and the "ladies" left the room. That really bothered me, considering the fact that one of these women had already had a child. The women were also all prudish and a bit controlling, while the men tended to be alcoholics. In short, I hated the male-female relationships on several levels. I can say, at least, that Eddings did make sure that his characters loved each other, but they were in such tight and confined relationship roles that I found every other aspect of the relationships stifling. I also was not super happy reading the part when Belgarath told Polgara should would have been a great son. NO. Just NO. I also had trouble dealing with peoples' eyes being "filled with wonder" or being a "mystery". I think it all just became too much for me. <br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I am sad because I think I am breaking up with these books; I have finally grown out of them for good. I am going to read through Belgarath the Sorcerer and Polgara the Sorceress one last time because I love the world Eddings made, but the good in this case just isn't able to compete with the annoyances I felt this time around. <br /><br />I will say that these books were fun for me when I was younger, and as a starter fantasy series, both the Belgariad and the Malloreon fit the bill. I also think the Belgariad is a much better series than the Malloreon, and many of these issues do not seem to be as prevalent in the Belgariad as they are in tme Malloreon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12690923232345356021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1091118593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10388375723538324457"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br/><b>Final rating - for the whole series ( <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/62114-belgarian-universe' rel='nofollow noopener'> Belgariad universe</a>): 5/5 stars</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>I started this series when i first bought first series <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/40739-the-belgariad' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Belgariad</a>, but it wasn't my favorite series back then. <br/><br/>I knew there was a sequel series, but i didn't rush to buy it (until all copies were almost sold, then i went into panic and bought the sequel as well). Reading the sequel series, The Malloreon, was unique experience. <br/><br/>The books were much longer, with more interesting story, and it was interes</span>
  <span id="freeText10388375723538324457" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br /><b>Final rating - for the whole series ( <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/62114-belgarian-universe" rel="nofollow noopener"> Belgariad universe</a>): 5/5 stars</b><br /><br /><br /><br />I started this series when i first bought first series <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40739-the-belgariad" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Belgariad</a>, but it wasn't my favorite series back then. <br /><br />I knew there was a sequel series, but i didn't rush to buy it (until all copies were almost sold, then i went into panic and bought the sequel as well). Reading the sequel series, The Malloreon, was unique experience. <br /><br />The books were much longer, with more interesting story, and it was interesting and funny read. Sad in some moments, but also very very funny. I don't remember i laughed that much anytime recently.<br />____________________________________________<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>OVERALL</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br />____________________________________________<br /><br />Overall, this whole universe, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/62114-belgarian-universe" rel="nofollow noopener"> Belgariad</a>, is worth reading once you get past the first five, also very very short, books. I liked them too, but i didn't love them as much as i love the sequel. In any case, this series is worth reading. <br /><br /><br />____________________________________________<br /><br />● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br />____________________________________________ <br /><br /><b>REVIEW(S) RELATED TO THIS BOOK:</b><br /><br />◈ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180264730" rel="nofollow noopener"> Pawn of Prophecy (The Belgariad #1) </a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="10388375723538324457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14384249866784580881">This is the last book in the Malloreon series and the end was definitely reading through the series if the characters have a special place in your heart. As much as I love the characters and the world that the story is set in I can't help but feel a little short changed with this series. It feels very much the same as the Belgariad series, just rehashed. To the point that the characters are commenting that so much that happens in this adventure mirrors the plot in the Belgaraid just with place n</span>
  <span id="freeText14384249866784580881" style="display:none">This is the last book in the Malloreon series and the end was definitely reading through the series if the characters have a special place in your heart. As much as I love the characters and the world that the story is set in I can't help but feel a little short changed with this series. It feels very much the same as the Belgariad series, just rehashed. To the point that the characters are commenting that so much that happens in this adventure mirrors the plot in the Belgaraid just with place name changes. I understand this was deliberate but I cant help feel that Eddings got a little lazy with ideas but wanted the characters to mature, grow and settle down living happily ever after.<br /><br />All that being said I would still recommend this to people that loved the first series. But if you only liked the Belgariad I would maybe steer clear of this later series as I feel you may just get annoyed.</span>

Once again Eddings grips us with his characters and ev</span>
  <span id="freeText4089494651511792564" style="display:none">This is the fifth and final in the Malloreon series and finds all the separate threads being brought together in an intense and epic finale that is worthy of the series as a whole. Every character faces their own challenges with Garion is deceived into wasting precious time following red herrings set by Naradas and Cyradis having to face the choice between Light and Dark without the aid of her trusted Toth, risking everything in the process. Once again Eddings grips us with his characters and even though deep down we know all will be well there is a small element of doubt that keeps you reading to the very end. A tried and tested series that adds nothing but good things to the world.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3276742954396797890">This is my review of both the Belgariad and the Malloreon. I read both through because I'm a sucker for a series about a long quest. However, it was nearly impossible to ignore the blatant misogyny and racism that permeated each and every book. He goes to needless lengths to make sure all his female characters - even the "strong" ones - are shown to be weak and "feminine" at least once or twice. And don't get me started on his description of non-white ethnicities. <br/><br/>The white male characters are a</span>
  <span id="freeText3276742954396797890" style="display:none">This is my review of both the Belgariad and the Malloreon. I read both through because I'm a sucker for a series about a long quest. However, it was nearly impossible to ignore the blatant misogyny and racism that permeated each and every book. He goes to needless lengths to make sure all his female characters - even the "strong" ones - are shown to be weak and "feminine" at least once or twice. And don't get me started on his description of non-white ethnicities. <br /><br />The white male characters are also fairly one-dimensional however, so with that balance, it was a fun though rather mindless swashbuckling romp through a strange little universe with an awful lot of gods and rules.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1562434401" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9008495847921553751">What a fantastic ending to a great series. The plot of the entire series comes to a head with shocking clarity. The way that all of the different parts of the story are wrapped up was rewarding. At the same time, the forward progression of the tale and the intricate world building never ceases. <br/><br/>The dynamic between the members of the group is so well defined by this point in the series that I felt as if I were part of it. Each individual has captured a piece of my heart throughout the series yet </span>
  <span id="freeText9008495847921553751" style="display:none">What a fantastic ending to a great series. The plot of the entire series comes to a head with shocking clarity. The way that all of the different parts of the story are wrapped up was rewarding. At the same time, the forward progression of the tale and the intricate world building never ceases. <br /><br />The dynamic between the members of the group is so well defined by this point in the series that I felt as if I were part of it. Each individual has captured a piece of my heart throughout the series yet they still managed to shine in unexpected ways throughout this novel. <br /><br />The ending of this novel was a bittersweet moment. It was a brilliant journey but I’m sad to see it end. <br /></span>

<div id="review_2391299535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2391299535" />
    <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos"><img alt="Sotiris Karaiskos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407195235p2/18940246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2391299535?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sotiris Karaiskos" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos">Sotiris Karaiskos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/12425052-the-seeress-of-kell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2391299535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15577898253763605058">In the fifth and last book of the series we do not have any particular surprises in relation to what we expect in this genre. Of course, it is through the ordinary something extraordinary can occur, and I think this is what the author does. The book begins in the same way that the previous one ended with our heroes wandering into the war zone trying to find the place of the final confrontation. Then we make a medieval break as knights, joustings and dangerous dragons invade our story. In the thi</span>
  <span id="freeText15577898253763605058" style="display:none">In the fifth and last book of the series we do not have any particular surprises in relation to what we expect in this genre. Of course, it is through the ordinary something extraordinary can occur, and I think this is what the author does. The book begins in the same way that the previous one ended with our heroes wandering into the war zone trying to find the place of the final confrontation. Then we make a medieval break as knights, joustings and dangerous dragons invade our story. In the third part we finally arrive at the final showdown which is as it should be in a epic fantasy work. Intense and adventurous, written in melodramatic tone, with a very delightful pompous style. The end of the book and the series is a long epilogue, which strangely does not become tiring, closes all the issues and offers an emotional and pleasant closure.<br /><br />A very good book that is the culmination of a very interesting epic fantasy series . The reading of the series was a very entertaining experience and it offered me some exciting moments. At the same time, it has a "historical" value, as did the author's previous series as a bridge to later works of the genre that he has clearly influenced. For these reasons I come to the end with very good impressions.<br /><br />Στο πέμπτο και τελευταίο βιβλίο της σειράς δεν συναντάμε ιδιαίτερες εκπλήξεις σε σχέση με αυτά που περιμένουμε σε αυτό το είδος. Φυσικά το ζητούμενο είναι μέσα από το συνηθισμένο να προκύπτει κάτι ασυνήθιστο και νομίζω ότι αυτό το καταφέρνει ο συγγραφέας. Το βιβλίο ξεκινάει με τον ίδιο τρόπο που τελείωσε το προηγούμενο με τους ήρωες μας να περιπλανώνται στην εμπόλεμη ζώνη ψάχνοντας να βρουν τον τόπο της τελικής αναμέτρησης. Στη συνέχεια κάνουμε ένα μεσαιωνικό διάλειμμα καθώς στην ιστορία μας εισβάλλουν ιππότες, κονταρομαχίες και επικίνδυνοι δράκοι. Στο τρίτο μέρος φτάνουμε επιτέλους στην τελική αναμέτρηση η οποία είναι όπως πρέπει να είναι σε ένα έργο επικής φαντασίας. Έντονη και περιπετειώδης, γραμμένη σε μελοδραματικό τόνο, με ένα ιδιαίτερα απολαυστικό πομπώδες ύφος. Το τέλος του βιβλίο και της σειράς είναι ένας μακρύς επίλογος, ο όποιος περιέργως δεν γίνεται καθόλου κουραστικός, κλείνει όλα τα εκκρεμή ζητήματα και προσφέρει ένα συναισθηματικό και ευχάριστο κλείσιμο.<br /><br />Ένα πολύ καλό βιβλίο που είναι το επιστέγασμα μιας πολύ ενδιαφέρουσας σειράς επικής φαντασίας. Η ανάγνωση της σειράς ήταν μία ιδιαίτερα διασκεδαστική εμπειρία και μου πρόσφερε και αρκετές συναρπαστικές στιγμές. Παράλληλα έχει και μία "ιστορική" αξία, όπως και η προηγούμενη σειρά του συγγραφέα λειτουργώντας ως μία γέφυρα προς τα μεταγενέστερα έργα του είδους τα οποία έχει σαφώς επηρεάσει. Για αυτούς τους λόγους φτάνω στο τέλος έχοντας πολύ καλές εντυπώσεις.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15577898253763605058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1847223194" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1847223194" />
    <a title="Ariana Fae" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29984848-ariana-fae"><img alt="Ariana Fae" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451784114p2/29984848.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1847223194?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ariana Fae" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ariana Fae" href="/user/show/29984848-ariana-fae">Ariana Fae</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/12425052-the-seeress-of-kell">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1847223194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5768267363053806158">As I finished the last book in David Eddings’ MALLOREON, I sat back and thought about the five books in the series. I like David Eddings and he one of the first fantasy authors I read growing up. I fell in love with his characters and their interactions with one another. I enjoyed the sense of humor, sarcasm, and wit each of them portrayed. I have fond memories of the BELGARIAD and the MALLOREON and think they are part of the golden age of fantasy, where heroes are good, villains are pure evil a</span>
  <span id="freeText5768267363053806158" style="display:none">As I finished the last book in David Eddings’ MALLOREON, I sat back and thought about the five books in the series. I like David Eddings and he one of the first fantasy authors I read growing up. I fell in love with his characters and their interactions with one another. I enjoyed the sense of humor, sarcasm, and wit each of them portrayed. I have fond memories of the BELGARIAD and the MALLOREON and think they are part of the golden age of fantasy, where heroes are good, villains are pure evil and there is a happy ending for those on the side of right.<br /><br />The MALLOREON series was good. I got to see the characters I love on another quest and get to know them better, and that’s why I re-visted this series. However as I listened to the stories I found myself drifting of at times. The MALLOREON is almost a recycled version of the BELGARIAD, and even in one of the chapters the characters make that same observation “that the same events seem to be repeating themselves”. Then there seem to unnecessary side trips with long winded conversations or drawn out scenes that slowed the pace of the story. We are also taken to off our hero’s quest to check in on minor characters, which in a way was interesting but not really necessary to the story. I found myself fast forwarding through many of them just to get the tale going forward again. <br /><br />With the fond memories I’ve had with the series, I was little disappointed that the re-vist didn’t live up to them. Although THE MALLOREON is not my favorite series out of David Eddings' collection, it was still an enjoyable read/listen. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5768267363053806158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15126853031772040428" style="display:none">With Lord of the Rings under my belt, I was hungry for more of this 'fantasy' thing I'd discovered. Enter the Belgariad. I consumed the two five-book series in a few months, getting in trouble in school for reading when I should have been paying attention (I either didn't care or had already done the homework for whatever it was they were teaching while they were teaching how to do it).<br /><br />When complete, I read the whole series again in half the time. Then again in half that. The half-lives continued until I read all ten books in slightly over a week then put them down forever as I drifted into the Shannaras.<br /><br />My copies of the books have long since wandered away; it would be interesting to read them again as currently all that remains in my memory are tiny snippets of demon summoner duels, walk walkers phasing people through stone, a pair of thousand-year old wizards tinkering in the affairs of nations, a feisty love interest, and the usual hapless teenageish boy that somehow ends up the hero of these things.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer155206375288067789">I have decided that the problem with the Mallorean is that it is too long. Three books would have been perfect rather than five, because ultimately the series is virtually the same as the Belgariad, but with the added bonus of trying to rescue Garion's son and the drawback that half the characters that you loved in the first series barely feature.<br/><br/>What I liked most about this last book is that the meeting between the Children of Light and Dark wraps up fairly quickly, leaving ample time to find o</span>
  <span id="freeText155206375288067789" style="display:none">I have decided that the problem with the Mallorean is that it is too long. Three books would have been perfect rather than five, because ultimately the series is virtually the same as the Belgariad, but with the added bonus of trying to rescue Garion's son and the drawback that half the characters that you loved in the first series barely feature.<br /><br />What I liked most about this last book is that the meeting between the Children of Light and Dark wraps up fairly quickly, leaving ample time to find out what happens to everyone afterwards. Something that you are often left to guess with a lot of books.<br /><br />I still struggled with the whole gender basis. Little boys get dirty just sleeping, women disapprove of drinking, love bathing and get emotional at romance etc, etc. You get the idea! It is a shame when all of the female characters are so strong, clever and very much the equals of the males.<br /><br />Don't let it put you off reading these series' though, as despite my complaining, I do love these characters and it has been nice getting to know them again. 4 stars</span>

  <span id="freeText8139738124413925388" style="display:none">A fun conclusion to a series that I've read over and over again. However, I have one specific problem with this book, which will be in Spoiler tags:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />The problem with this book is the choice that Cyradis has to make. At no point does Cyradis act like she has any inclination to choose the dark. At no point are we convinced that she will choose the dark. <div id="review_3561857822" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3561857822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18197869766549984095">I truly hate when a good book let alone a series ends. You get invested not only in the characters but also in the narrative each author has their own voice and after ten books it's going to be awkward to get into someone else's way of writing. Eddings does a very good job of character interaction. Humor is high on the list and even in the midst of battle a moment can be found to interject a humorous comment. There's a feeling of. . . humanity, vulnerability, flaws in each person he created for </span>
  <span id="freeText18197869766549984095" style="display:none">I truly hate when a good book let alone a series ends. You get invested not only in the characters but also in the narrative each author has their own voice and after ten books it's going to be awkward to get into someone else's way of writing. Eddings does a very good job of character interaction. Humor is high on the list and even in the midst of battle a moment can be found to interject a humorous comment. There's a feeling of. . . humanity, vulnerability, flaws in each person he created for us.<br />To the ends of the world Garion and his companions traveled, to the final meeting of the Child of Light and the Child of Dark all hinged on the simple choice of a seeress of Kell.<br />I laughed out loud numerous times. I cried a couple of times as well (yeah, I'm still an emotional wreck sometimes) and that's the mark of good story telling.<br />We did get a decent 'and they lived happily ever after' epilogue at the end. Not quite as long as Tolkien did at the end of TLotR but wound things up nicely.<br />I highly recommend the series, yeah it did drag out a little in the middle but it reads easily and smoothly so, dive in. I think you'll like this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18197869766549984095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer13804289635212317353">There wasn’t anything that wasn’t predictable, but it was still a fun adventure. I did like the unique way the heroes went against the second-in-command villain. The epilogue tried to match Return of the King with the several different ending scenes. Overall, this wasn’t as good as the Belgariad, but it was much better than Elenium. </span>

<div id="review_20648313" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20648313" />
    <a title="Stacey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1065875-stacey"><img alt="Stacey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232913448p2/1065875.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20648313?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey" href="/user/show/1065875-stacey">Stacey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345377593" href="/book/show/773523.The_Seeress_of_Kell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1065875-stacey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20648313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4327081124339652919">A reread after a decade away<br/>Garion & company, now including the Emporer Kal Zakath himself, head out for Kell to meet up with Cyradis and at long last learn where the Place That is No More actually is. But the various factions arrayed against them cannot go to Kell, so they are all waiting to pounce.<br/>The trip to Kell sends them to the island of Perivor, which is only technically Mallorean. It was settled 2000 years ago by some Mimbrate Arends who got blown off course & their fierce warlike nature</span>
  <span id="freeText4327081124339652919" style="display:none">A reread after a decade away<br />Garion &amp; company, now including the Emporer Kal Zakath himself, head out for Kell to meet up with Cyradis and at long last learn where the Place That is No More actually is. But the various factions arrayed against them cannot go to Kell, so they are all waiting to pounce.<br />The trip to Kell sends them to the island of Perivor, which is only technically Mallorean. It was settled 2000 years ago by some Mimbrate Arends who got blown off course &amp; their fierce warlike nature means no one has really tried to take control of the island by force. Zandramas' henchman Naradas tries his best to keep them there &amp; from learning the true location of Korim where the final, final, we really mean it this time, contest between the two prophecies will happen, for good. (oh sure we've imported the idea to the Elenium &amp; the Tamuli but as far as this world is concerned it really will be over)<br />There are some peculiar continuity errors I only caught because I reread Belgarath the Sorcerer before this. In Belgarath, it's him that knows Old Angarak and he has to teach Beldin enough to spot copies of some book or other. But in Seeress it's Beldin that knows Old Angarak best and Belgarath who struggles with it. Polgara is also called an Alorn throughout this series, but in Belgarath we're told he doesn't even know which god his people worshipped before he met Aldur and his wife, Poledra, is a wolf who shape changed into a woman. So how can Polgara be an Alorn?<br />It's the usual great story, with entertaining witty dialogue and some casual sexism &amp; Polgara and her misandry, thrown in. I enjoyed it as usual.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4327081124339652919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_511017126" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/511017126" />
    <a title="Gareth Otton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8925316-gareth-otton"><img alt="Gareth Otton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551041676p2/8925316.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/511017126?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gareth Otton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gareth Otton" href="/user/show/8925316-gareth-otton">Gareth Otton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer511017126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15458074215389743200">This is a review for the series as a whole and not just for this book. <br/><br/>There are a lot of negatives to the Malloreon, it is long winded, often slow and very repetitive, but I feel that the positives of this series are more significant. <br/><br/>In the Malloreon, David Eddings nicely rounds off what he started in the Belgariad. It was often very philosophical and at times a bit too wordy but at the end you cant help but grin as these characters you have come to love over the previous ten books get their h</span>
  <span id="freeText15458074215389743200" style="display:none">This is a review for the series as a whole and not just for this book. <br /><br />There are a lot of negatives to the Malloreon, it is long winded, often slow and very repetitive, but I feel that the positives of this series are more significant. <br /><br />In the Malloreon, David Eddings nicely rounds off what he started in the Belgariad. It was often very philosophical and at times a bit too wordy but at the end you cant help but grin as these characters you have come to love over the previous ten books get their happily ever after. <br /><br />Both series will never sit on high as the best novels of all time, nor even the greatest fantasy series. They are too flawed to ever be there but they are also brilliant in their own right. You can't help but feel the same kind of love for these books as you do for your favourite sitcom on television, it is not ground breaking TV but you love it none the less. <br /><br />All in all a fantastic series and even after three readings I love them still. <br /><br />A final word of warning to first time readers though, be wary of the prequels to this series (Belgarath the Sorcerer and Polgara the sorceress) as they do little to add to this story. Belgarath the sorcerer has its moments but all that either book really does is retell a history that we already know from reading these books but in more (and sometimes contrasting) detail.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15458074215389743200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EwvnYcPPjakr1CUAYYlszENRTkUmVPJJPT7WCGvLiakXGwEIsvPQyBN16gmX1ySxb4NXSgwzY3bMaW2/N3wQhA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aAWjm2RJcES/c3fYyMS1d9+8aszyvIk5J9m4GHaKP0xsFUXyFXUtJYfSuNE+mv0K825zw9jbGAbWjgOvKj2mYQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15004759350790258529">David Eddings was an American author who wrote several best-selling series of epic fantasy novels. David Eddings' wife, <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8732.Leigh_Eddings' title='Leigh Eddings' rel='nofollow noopener'>Leigh Eddings</a>
</b>, was an uncredited co-author on many of his early books, but he had later acknowledged that she contributed to them all.<br/><br/>David Eddings' first books (which were general fiction) sold moderately well. He later switched to writing epic fantasy, a field in which he a</span>
  <span id="freeText15004759350790258529" style="display:none">David Eddings was an American author who wrote several best-selling series of epic fantasy novels. David Eddings' wife, <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8732.Leigh_Eddings" title="Leigh Eddings" rel="nofollow noopener">Leigh Eddings</a>
</b>, was an uncredited co-author on many of his early books, but he had later acknowledged that she contributed to them all.<br /><br />David Eddings' first books (which were general fiction) sold moderately well. He later switched to writing epic fantasy, a field in which he achieved great success. In a recent interview with sffworld.com, he said: "I don't take orders from readers."<br /><br />On January 26, 2007 it was reported that Eddings accidentally burned about a quarter of his office, next door to his house, along with his Excalibur sports car, and the original manuscripts for most of his novels. He was flushing the fuel tank of the car with water when he lit a piece of paper and threw into the puddle to test if it was still flammable.<br /><br />On February 28, 2007, David Eddings' wife, Leigh Eddings (born Judith Leigh Schall), died following a series of strokes. She was 69.<br /><br />David Eddings died on June 2, 2009 at the age of 77.</span>
